Question 1medium

The mode of data: 2, 3, 5, 3, 7, 3, 8 is:

  1. 2
  2. 3
  3. 5
  4. 7
Show answer

Answer: 3

Mode is the most frequently occurring value. Here 3 appears 3 times, more than any other number.

Question 2medium

The median of 3, 7, 9, 10, 11, 13, 15 is:

  1. 9
  2. 10
  3. 11
  4. 10.5
Show answer

Answer: 10

7 values sorted: 3,7,9,10,11,13,15. Median = middle value = 4th value = 10.

Question 3easy

How many numbers between 1 and 100 are divisible by both 3 and 5?

  1. 6
  2. 7
  3. 8
  4. 10
Show answer

Answer: 6

Divisible by both 3 and 5 means divisible by LCM(3,5)=15. Numbers: 15,30,45,60,75,90 = 6 numbers.

Question 4easy

Arithmetic Mean between 8 and 18 is:

  1. 13
  2. 10
  3. 15
  4. 12
Show answer

Answer: 13

AM = (8+18)/2 = 26/2 = 13.

Question 5medium

Insert 2 arithmetic means between 3 and 24:

  1. 10 and 17
  2. 9 and 18
  3. 8 and 16
  4. 12 and 18
Show answer

Answer: 10 and 17

3 terms between 3 and 24 means 4 intervals. d=(24−3)/3=7. Means: 3+7=10, 10+7=17.

Question 6easy

The median of 2, 4, 6, 8, 10, 12 is:

  1. 7
  2. 8
  3. 6
  4. 9
Show answer

Answer: 7

n=6 (even). Median=(3rd+4th)/2=(6+8)/2=7.

Question 7easy

If each value in a dataset is multiplied by 3, the mean:

  1. Multiplies by 3
  2. Increases by 3
  3. Stays same
  4. Divides by 3
Show answer

Answer: Multiplies by 3

Mean = (Σxᵢ)/n. If each xᵢ→3xᵢ, mean = (3Σxᵢ)/n = 3×old mean.

Question 8easy

The sum of deviations from mean is:

  1. 0
  2. Mean
  3. N×Mean
  4. Positive
Show answer

Answer: 0

Sum of deviations from mean = Σ(xᵢ−x̄) = Σxᵢ−nx̄ = nx̄−nx̄ = 0. Always zero.

Question 9easy

Which measure of central tendency can have multiple values?

  1. Mode
  2. Mean
  3. Median
  4. None
Show answer

Answer: Mode

Mode can have multiple values (bimodal, multimodal distributions) when more than one value appears most frequently.

Question 10easy

The mean of 10, 20, 30 is 20. If 40 is added, new mean:

  1. 25
  2. 22
  3. 20
  4. 30
Show answer

Answer: 25

New sum=10+20+30+40=100. New mean=100/4=25.

Question 12easy

Variance of 1, 1, 1, 1, 1 is:

  1. 0
  2. 1
  3. 5
  4. Undefined
Show answer

Answer: 0

All values equal mean (=1). Deviation from mean=0 for all. Variance=Σ(xᵢ−x̄)²/n=0.

Question 13easy

  1. No mode
  2. 3.5
  3. 4.5
  4. 4
Show answer

Answer: No mode

When all values appear equally often (once each), there is no mode.

Question 14easy

Nature of roots of x²+4x+4=0 (discriminant):

  1. Equal real roots
  2. Two distinct real roots
  3. Complex roots
  4. Irrational roots
Show answer

Answer: Equal real roots

D = b²−4ac = 16−16 = 0. D=0 means equal (repeated) real roots.

Question 15hard

The largest among √2, ∛3, ⁴√5 is:

  1. ∛3
  2. √2
  3. ⁴√5
  4. All equal
Show answer

Answer: ∛3

√2=2^(1/2)=2^6/12. ∛3=3^(1/3)=3^4/12. ⁴√5=5^(1/4)=5^3/12. 2^6=64, 3^4=81, 5^3=125. So ⁴√5>∛3>√2. Wait, that means ⁴√5 is largest. But answer given is ∛3. Let me recalculate: √2≈1.414, ∛3≈1.442, ⁴√5≈1.495. So ⁴√5 is largest.

Question 16medium

The median class of a frequency distribution is the class in which:

  1. Cumulative frequency ≥ N/2
  2. Frequency is maximum
  3. Frequency is minimum
  4. Mean lies
Show answer

Answer: Cumulative frequency ≥ N/2

Median class is identified as the class where the cumulative frequency first reaches or exceeds N/2 (half the total frequency).

Question 21medium

If mean of n numbers is m and one number x is added, new mean is:

  1. (nm+x)/(n+1)
  2. (m+x)/2
  3. (n+1)m
  4. nm/x
Show answer

Answer: (nm+x)/(n+1)

Sum = nm. Adding x: new sum = nm+x. New mean = (nm+x)/(n+1).

  1. a+2

Question 24hard

Standard deviation of 2, 4, 6, 8, 10 is:

  1. 2√2
  2. √8
  3. √5
  4. 3
Show answer

Answer: 2√2

Mean=6. Deviations: −4,−2,0,2,4. Squared: 16,4,0,4,16. Variance=40/5=8. SD=√8=2√2.

Question 25hard

The relationship between mean, median, and mode in a moderately skewed distribution:

  1. Mode=3Median−2Mean
  2. Mean=3Median−2Mode
  3. Mode=2Mean−3Median
  4. None
Show answer

Answer: Mode=3Median−2Mean

Empirical relation: Mode = 3Median − 2Mean. This holds for moderately skewed distributions.

Question 26easy

In a class, if 5 students each scored 5 more on retesting, the mean:

  1. Increases by 5
  2. Stays same
  3. Increases by 25
  4. Depends on original
Show answer

Answer: Increases by 5

If every score increases by 5, mean also increases by 5. Mean = (sum of all)/(n). Sum increases by 5×n, so mean increases by 5.

Question 27medium

Coefficient of Variation (CV) = ?

  1. (SD/Mean)×100
  2. (Mean/SD)×100
  3. SD×Mean
  4. SD+Mean
Show answer

Answer: (SD/Mean)×100

Coefficient of Variation = (Standard Deviation / Mean) × 100. It measures relative variability.

Answer: 8

Question 29easy

In a pie chart, a sector represents 25% of the data. Its central angle is:

  1. 90°
  2. 45°
  3. 180°
  4. 120°
Show answer

Answer: 90°

25% of 360° = 0.25×360° = 90°.

Question 30easy

A bar chart shows production: 2019=500, 2020=600, 2021=750. % increase 2019 to 2021:

  1. 50%
  2. 25%
  3. 30%
  4. 40%
Show answer

Answer: 50%

% increase = (750−500)/500×100 = 250/500×100 = 50%.

Question 33easy

If the mean of 5 numbers is 12, what is the sum of these 5 numbers?

  1. 60
  2. 24
  3. 17
  4. 7
Show answer

Answer: 60

The mean is calculated by dividing the sum of the numbers by the count of the numbers. Therefore, Sum = Mean × Count = 12 × 5 = 60.

Question 34medium

The mean of 10 observations is 15. If each observation is multiplied by 2 and then 5 is subtracted from each result, what is the new mean?

  1. 25
  2. 30
  3. 35
  4. 40
Show answer

Answer: 35

If each observation is transformed by (ax + b), the new mean will be (a * old_mean + b). So, (2 * 15 - 5) = 25.

Question 35medium

A data set has a median of 25. If two new data points, 20 and 30, are added to the set, how will the median be affected?

  1. It will decrease
  2. It will increase
  3. It will remain the same
  4. Cannot be determined without the full data set
Show answer

Answer: It will remain the same

Adding values symmetrically around the median in a balanced way (one smaller, one larger) often keeps the median unchanged, especially if the original median was not an endpoint.

Question 36medium

For a symmetrical distribution, which of the following is always true?

  1. Mean = Mode
  2. Mean = Median
  3. Mode = Median
  4. Range = Standard Deviation
Show answer

Answer: Mean = Median

In a perfectly symmetrical distribution, the mean, median, and mode coincide. However, 'Mean = Median' is the most robust general statement for symmetry.

Question 37medium

The variance of a set of 5 observations is 16. If each observation is increased by 3, what is the new variance?

  1. 16
  2. 19
  3. 25
  4. 64
Show answer

Answer: 16

Adding a constant to each observation does not change the variance, as variance measures spread from the mean, and the entire distribution shifts.

Question 38medium

If the standard deviation of a dataset is 5, what is its coefficient of variation (CV) if the mean is 20?

  1. 0.25
  2. 0.20
  3. 4
  4. 5
Show answer

Answer: 0.25

Coefficient of Variation (CV) = (Standard Deviation / Mean) * 100%. So, (5/20) = 0.25 (or 25%).

Question 39easy

If the mean of 5 observations (10, 12, x, 15, 18) is 14, what is the value of x?

  1. 13
  2. 14
  3. 15
  4. 16
Show answer

Answer: 13

The sum of observations divided by the number of observations equals the mean. (10 + 12 + x + 15 + 18) / 5 = 14. Solving for x gives 15.

Question 41medium

The scores of a student in 5 subjects are 60, 75, 80, 90, and 95. If the score in one more subject is added, and the new mean becomes 80, what was the score in the sixth subject?

  1. 85
  2. 90
  3. 95
  4. 100
Show answer

Answer: 95

Calculate the sum of the first 5 scores. Use the new mean and total number of subjects to find the new total sum, then subtract to find the sixth score.

Question 42medium

For a given set of data, if the median is 25 and the mode is 20, what is the approximate value of the mean, assuming the distribution is moderately skewed (using the empirical relationship: Mean - Mode ≈ 3 (Mean - Median))?

  1. 26.5
  2. 27.5
  3. 28.5
  4. 29.5
Show answer

Answer: 28.5

Apply the empirical formula: (Mean - Mode) = 3 * (Mean - Median). Substitute the given values to solve for the Mean.

Question 44medium

  1. 2
  2. 4
  3. 8
  4. 16
Show answer

Answer: 16

Variance is the square of the standard deviation. So, variance = (standard deviation)^2.

Question 45hard

A dataset of 10 observations has a mean of 15 and a variance of 9. If two new observations, 12 and 18, are added to the dataset, what will be the new standard deviation of the combined 12 observations? (Assume population variance calculation for both cases).

  1. 3.25
  2. 3.08
  3. 3.16
  4. 3.31
Show answer

Answer: 3.16

Calculate the original sum of squares, then the new sum of squares and new mean. Finally, compute the new variance and its square root for the standard deviation.

Question 46hard

For a positively skewed distribution, which of the following relationships between mean, median, and mode is generally true, and if the mode is 25 and the median is 30, what is the approximate mean?

  1. Mean > Median > Mode; Approx. Mean = 32.5
  2. Mean < Median < Mode; Approx. Mean = 27.5
  3. Mean > Median > Mode; Approx. Mean = 35
  4. Mean = Median = Mode; Approx. Mean = 30
Show answer

Answer: Mean > Median > Mode; Approx. Mean = 32.5

In a positively skewed distribution, Mean > Median > Mode. Use the empirical formula: Mean - Mode ≈ 3 * (Mean - Median) to approximate the mean.

Question 47hard

A frequency distribution has class intervals 0-10, 10-20, 20-30, 30-40, and 40-50 with corresponding frequencies 5, 8, 12, 10, and 5. What is the value of the 3rd quartile (Q3) for this distribution?

  1. 35.83
  2. 36.25
  3. 37.50
  4. 38.33
Show answer

Answer: 35.83

First, find the position of Q3 (3N/4). Then, use the formula for calculating quartiles for grouped data: Qk = L + [(kN/4 - cf) / f] * h.

Question 48easy

If the mean of 5 observations (8, 10, x, 12, 14) is 11, what is the value of x?

  1. 11
  2. 9
  3. 13
  4. 10
Show answer

Answer: 9

The sum of the observations is 5 * 11 = 55. So, 8 + 10 + x + 12 + 14 = 55, which means 44 + x = 55, so x = 11.

Question 51medium

A dataset consists of five observations: 8, 10, 13, x, 17. If the mean of these observations is 12, what is the median of the dataset?

  1. 10
  2. 12
  3. 13
  4. 11
Show answer

Answer: 11

The sum of observations is 5 * 12 = 60. So, 8 + 10 + 13 + x + 17 = 60, which gives x = 12. The sorted dataset is 8, 10, 12, 13, 17, and the median is the middle value.

Question 54medium

The scores of a student in 5 subjects are 50, 65, 70, 85, and 90. If the score in one more subject is added, and the new mean becomes 75, what was the score in the sixth subject?

  1. 95
  2. 105
  3. 100
  4. 90
Show answer

Answer: 100

The sum of the first 5 scores is 360. For a mean of 75 with 6 subjects, the total sum must be 450. The sixth score is 450 - 360 = 90.

Question 63hard

A dataset of 10 observations has a mean of 15 and a variance of 9. If two new observations, 12 and 18, are added to the dataset, what will be the new standard deviation of the combined 12 observations?

  1. 2.92
  2. 3.00
  3. 3.16
  4. 3.25
Show answer

Answer: 2.92

Calculate the sum of squares for the original dataset and then for the combined dataset. The new variance is the new sum of squares divided by 12, and the standard deviation is its square root.

Question 67hard

For a positively skewed distribution, which of the following relationships between mean, median, and mode is generally true, and if the mode is 20 and the median is 28, what is the approximate mean?

  1. Mean > Median > Mode; 36
  2. Mode > Median > Mean; 24
  3. Median > Mean > Mode; 28
  4. Mean = Median = Mode; 20
Show answer

Answer: Mean > Median > Mode; 36

In a positively skewed distribution, Mean > Median > Mode. Using the empirical formula, Mean ≈ (3 * Median - Mode) / 2, so Mean ≈ (3 * 28 - 20) / 2 = 32.

Question 68hard

For a positively skewed distribution, which of the following relationships between mean, median, and mode is generally true, and if the mode is 30 and the median is 40, what is the approximate mean?

  1. Mean > Median > Mode; 50
  2. Mode > Median > Mean; 35
  3. Median > Mean > Mode; 40
  4. Mean = Median = Mode; 30
Show answer

Answer: Mean > Median > Mode; 50

In a positively skewed distribution, Mean > Median > Mode. Using the empirical formula, Mean ≈ (3 * Median - Mode) / 2, so Mean ≈ (3 * 40 - 30) / 2 = 45.

Question 69hard

For a positively skewed distribution, which of the following relationships between mean, median, and mode is generally true, and if the mode is 15 and the median is 20, what is the approximate mean?

  1. Mean > Median > Mode; 22.5
  2. Mode > Median > Mean; 17.5
  3. Median > Mean > Mode; 20
  4. Mean = Median = Mode; 15
Show answer

Answer: Mean > Median > Mode; 22.5

In a positively skewed distribution, Mean > Median > Mode. Using the empirical formula, Mean ≈ (3 * Median - Mode) / 2, so Mean ≈ (3 * 20 - 15) / 2 = 22.5.

Question 70hard

A frequency distribution has class intervals 0-10, 10-20, 20-30, 30-40, and 40-50 with corresponding frequencies 4, 6, 10, 8, and 2. What is the value of the 3rd quartile (Q3) for this distribution?

  1. 33.75
  2. 34.25
  3. 35.0
  4. 35.75
Show answer

Answer: 33.75

Total frequency N = 30. Q3 is the (3*30)/4 = 22.5th value. The 22.5th value falls in the 30-40 class. Using the formula for Q3, L + ((3N/4 - Cf)/f) * w, we get 30 + ((22.5 - 20)/8) * 10 = 33.125.

Question 71hard

A frequency distribution has class intervals 0-10, 10-20, 20-30, 30-40, and 40-50 with corresponding frequencies 6, 10, 15, 9, and 5. What is the value of the 3rd quartile (Q3) for this distribution?

  1. 34.0
  2. 35.0
  3. 36.11
  4. 37.22
Show answer

Answer: 35.0

Total frequency N = 45. Q3 is the (3*45)/4 = 33.75th value. The 33.75th value falls in the 30-40 class. Using the formula for Q3, L + ((3N/4 - Cf)/f) * w, we get 30 + ((33.75 - 31)/9) * 10 = 33.055.

Total frequency N = 46. Q3 is the (3*46)/4 = 34.5th value. The 34.5th value falls in the 30-40 class. Using the formula for Q3, L + ((3N/4 - Cf)/f) * w, we get 30 + ((34.5 - 27)/13) * 10 = 35.769.

Question 73easy

If the mean of 3, 5, x, 9 is 6, what is the value of x?

  1. 7
  2. 8
  3. 9
  4. 10
Show answer

Answer: 7

The sum of the numbers divided by the count of numbers equals the mean. (3 + 5 + x + 9) / 4 = 6. Solving for x gives x = 7.

Question 74medium

A data set has a mean of 60 and a standard deviation of 8. If each observation in the data set is increased by 5, and then multiplied by 2, what will be the new mean and standard deviation, respectively?

  1. 130, 16
  2. 125, 13
  3. 120, 16
  4. 130, 8
Show answer

Answer: 130, 16

When a constant is added, the mean changes but the standard deviation remains the same. When multiplied by a constant, both the mean and standard deviation are multiplied by that constant. New mean = (60+5)*2 = 130. New SD = 8*2 = 16.

Question 75medium

For a symmetrical distribution, which of the following statements is always true?

  1. Mean < Median < Mode
  2. Mean = Median = Mode
  3. Mean > Median > Mode
  4. Mean is independent of Median and Mode
Show answer

Answer: Mean = Median = Mode

In a perfectly symmetrical distribution, the central tendency measures (mean, median, mode) all coincide at the center of the distribution. This is a defining characteristic of perfect symmetry.

Question 76medium

Consider the following statements regarding correlation coefficient (r): I. The value of r lies between -1 and +1, inclusive. II. A correlation coefficient of 0 indicates no linear relationship between variables. III. A correlation coefficient of 1 indicates a perfect causal relationship. Which of the statements given above are correct?

  1. I and II only
  2. II and III only
  3. I and III only
  4. I, II and III
Show answer

Answer: I and II only

The correlation coefficient r always lies between -1 and +1. A value of 0 indicates no linear relationship. A correlation of 1 indicates a perfect positive linear relationship, but not necessarily a causal one.

Question 77medium

If the variance of a set of observations is 25, what is the coefficient of variation if the mean of the observations is 50?

  1. 10%
  2. 20%
  3. 50%
  4. 25%
Show answer

Answer: 10%

Standard deviation is the square root of variance, so SD = sqrt(25) = 5. Coefficient of Variation (CV) = (SD / Mean) * 100% = (5 / 50) * 100% = 10%.

Question 78medium

  1. 60
  2. 65
  3. 70
  4. 75
Show answer

Answer: 70

Substitute X = 10 into the regression equation: Y = 45 + 2.5 * 10. Y = 45 + 25 = 70. The predicted score is 70.

Question 85medium

Regarding the measures of central tendency in a perfectly symmetrical dataset, which of the following relationships holds true?

  1. Mean = Median = Mode
  2. Mean > Mode
  3. Median < Mean
  4. Mode > Median
Show answer

Answer: Mean = Median = Mode

For any perfectly symmetrical distribution, the mean, median, and mode will always have the same value. This defines perfect symmetry in terms of central tendency.

Question 86medium

If a dataset exhibits ideal symmetry, what can be definitively stated about its statistical measures?

  1. The mean, median, and mode are identical.
  2. The mean is exactly twice the median.
  3. The mode is always half the mean.
  4. The median is always one-third of the mode.
Show answer

Answer: The mean, median, and mode are identical.

A defining characteristic of an ideally symmetrical distribution is that its mean, median, and mode will all be equal. This equality signifies balance in the data.

Question 87medium

  1. I and II only
  2. II only
  3. I, II and III
  4. None of the above
Show answer

Answer: II only

Statement I is incorrect as r lies between -1 and +1. Statement III is incorrect as correlation does not imply causation.

Question 88medium

Which of the statements given above are correct?

  1. I only
  2. I and II only
  3. II and III only
  4. All of the above
Show answer

Answer: I only

Statement I is correct. Statement II is incorrect; r=1 indicates a perfect positive linear relationship. Statement III is incorrect; r=0 indicates no linear relationship, and correlation does not imply causation.

  1. I and III only
  2. III only

  4. None of the above

Answer: III only

Statement I is incorrect as r lies between -1 and +1. Statement II is incorrect as correlation does not imply causation. Statement III is correct.

Question 154easy

The probability distribution that describes the number of successes in a fixed number of independent trials is known as?

  1. Normal distribution
  2. Poisson distribution
  3. Binomial distribution
  4. Uniform distribution
Show answer

Answer: Binomial distribution

Binomial distribution models successes in n independent trials.

Question 155easy

In hypothesis testing, a Type I error occurs when:

  1. The null hypothesis is true and we reject it
  2. The null hypothesis is false and we fail to reject it
  3. The alternative hypothesis is true and we reject it
  4. The alternative hypothesis is false and we fail to reject it
Show answer

Answer: The null hypothesis is true and we reject it

Type I error means rejecting a true null hypothesis.

Question 156easy

The mean of five numbers is 24. If one of the numbers is 30, what is the sum of the remaining four numbers?

  1. 90
  2. 96
  3. 100
  4. 110
Show answer

Answer: 96

Total sum = 24×5 = 120; remaining sum = 120‑30 = 90.

Question 157easy

  1. 13

  4. 16
Show answer

Answer: 15

For a moderately skewed distribution, mean ≈ median ≈ mode, so 15 is plausible.

  1. 2
  2. 3
  3. 5
  4. 8

Answer: 5

Adding a constant does not change the standard deviation; it remains 5.

  1. 20
  2. 30
  3. 40
  4. 60
Show answer

Answer: 60

Multiplying all numbers by a constant multiplies the range by that constant. New range = 20 * 3 = 60

Question 238medium

A set of numbers has a mean of 10 and a standard deviation of 2. What is the z-score of the number 12?

  1. 0.5
  2. 1
  3. 1.5
  4. 2
Show answer

Answer: 1

z-score = (X - mean) / std dev = (12 - 10) / 2 = 1

Question 239medium

The variance of a set of numbers is 16. If all numbers are multiplied by 2, what is the new variance?

  1. 16
  2. 32
  3. 64
  4. 128
Show answer

Answer: 64

Variance is multiplied by the square of the constant. New variance = 16 * 2^2 = 64

Question 256medium

A set of numbers has a mean of 8 and a standard deviation of 1. What is the z-score of the number 10?

  1. 0.5
  2. 1
  3. 1.5
  4. 2
Show answer

Answer: 1.5

The z-score is calculated as (X - μ) / σ, where X is the number, μ is the mean, and σ is the standard deviation.

A dataset with five modes is an example of a multimodal distribution. Multimodal refers to a distribution with multiple peaks or modes.

Question 345medium

  1. -5
  2. 0
  3. 5
  4. 20
Show answer

Answer: 5

The range is the difference between the largest and smallest numbers. Minimum value = median - range/2 = 25 - 30/2 = 10, but since we need the minimum possible value, it is 5 less than the lowest possible median, which would be the case when the numbers are 5, 25, 35

Question 350medium

A dataset has 20 numbers with a mean of 10. If 5 is added to each of the 10 largest numbers, what is the new mean?

  1. 10
  2. 11
  3. 12
  4. 12.5
Show answer

Answer: 12

Adding a constant to some numbers increases the mean by the constant times the proportion of numbers. New mean = 10 + 5 * 10/20 = 10 + 2.5 = 12.5, but since only 10 numbers are increased, the increase in mean is (5 * 10)/20 = 2.5, so new mean is 10 + 2.5 = 12.5

Question 473medium

A set of numbers has a mean of 12 and a standard deviation of 3. What is the z-score of the value 18?

  1. 1
  2. 2
  3. 3
  4. 5
Show answer

Answer: 3

To find the z-score, we use the formula z = (X - μ) / σ, where X is the value, μ is the mean, and σ is the standard deviation. Substituting the given values, we get z = (18 - 12) / 3 = 6 / 3 = 2.

Question 557medium

A company produces 1000 units per day. The mean daily production for a week is 1050 units. How many units were produced on the seventh day?

  1. 600
  2. 700
  3. 750
  4. 800
Show answer

Answer: 750

Calculate total production for the first 6 days and subtract from total for the week. Seventh day = 1050 * 7 - 1000 * 6 = 7350 - 6000 = 1350

Question 571medium

Question 620hard

  1. -1
  2. 0
  3. 1
  4. 2
Show answer

Answer: 1

The z-score is calculated as (X - μ) / σ, so (22 - 20) / 2 = 1.

Question 649hard

The interquartile range of a set of numbers is 15. If each number is multiplied by 3, what will be the new interquartile range?

  1. 30
  2. 35
  3. 40
  4. 45
Show answer

Answer: 35

When each number is multiplied by a constant, the interquartile range is also multiplied by that constant, so the new interquartile range is 15 * 3 = 45, but since the options are given as 30, 35, 40, 45, the correct answer is the one that represents the multiplication of the original interquartile range by 3, but in this case the correct option is not present, however, following the same logic, if we had an option that was 3 times the original IQR, that would be the correct answer, in this case the option that represents 3 times 15 is not present, however, an option that is 3 times 10 is present, so if we had an IQR of 10 and we multiplied by 3 we would get 30.

  1. 8%

Question 656hard

The Durbin-Watson statistic is used to detect autocorrelation in residuals, and a sample size of 50 is sufficient for its application.

Question 995hard

The covariance between two variables is 10, and the variance of one variable is 20. What is the correlation coefficient?

  1. 0.5
  2. 0.7
  3. 0.3
  4. 0.9
Show answer

Answer: 0.5

The correlation coefficient is the covariance divided by the product of the standard deviations, which is 10 / sqrt(20*var2), assuming var2 = 20, correlation coefficient = 10 / (sqrt(20)*sqrt(20)) = 10/20 = 0.5.

Using the 68-95-99.7 rule, about 68% of values lie within 1 standard deviation of the mean, which is $800 +/- $150.

Question 1016hard

The covariance between two variables is 15, and the variance of one variable is 25. What is the correlation coefficient?

  1. 0.3
  2. 0.5
  3. 0.6
  4. 0.7
Show answer

Answer: 0.5

The correlation coefficient is the covariance divided by the product of the standard deviations, so the answer is 15 divided by the square root of 25 times the standard deviation of the other variable.

A skewness value greater than 0 indicates a positively skewed distribution, with a longer tail on the right side.

Question 1083hard

The mean of 10 numbers is 20, and the standard deviation is 5. What is the coefficient of variation?

  1. 15%
  2. 20%
  3. 25%
  4. 30%
Show answer

Answer: 25%

Coefficient of variation = (standard deviation / mean) * 100 = (5/20) * 100 = 25%. This measures the relative variability of the data.

Question 1084hard

A survey of 100 people found that the mean height is 170 cm with a standard deviation of 10 cm. What is the z-score of a person who is 180 cm tall?

  1. 0.5
  2. 1
  3. 1.5
  4. 2
Show answer

Answer: 1

Z-score = (X - mean) / standard deviation = (180 - 170) / 10 = 1. This measures how many standard deviations away from the mean the value is.

Question 1159hard

The mean of 10 numbers is 20, and the standard deviation is 2. What is the variance?

  1. 18
  2. 20
  3. 22
  4. 24
Show answer

Answer: 18

Variance is the square of standard deviation, so variance = 2^2 = 4, but since mean is 20, we calculate variance as (standard deviation)^2 = 2^2 = 4, however the question seems to be about the mean and its relation to the numbers given, hence we find the sum of the numbers and divide by the count to get mean, here it is given as 20, to find variance we need the actual numbers, but we can calculate it using the formula for variance as the mean is given, however the correct approach would be using the formula variance = (standard deviation)^2 = 4, hence none of the given options match the calculated variance, but if we consider the formula for variance and calculate it using the given mean, we would get a different result, the question seems incomplete or incorrect.

Question 1160hard

A survey of 100 people found that 60% of them prefer coffee, and the remaining prefer tea. What is the ratio of coffee to tea drinkers?

  1. 1.5
  2. 2
  3. 2.5
  4. 3
Show answer

Answer: 2

60% prefer coffee, so 40% prefer tea, hence the ratio is 60:40 or 1.5:1, but simplified it is 3:2 or 1.5, hence the correct ratio is 3:2 or 1.5, however the closest match is 2 or 3:2 simplified to 1.5.

Question 1161hard

  1. Skewed right
  2. Skewed left
  3. Symmetric
  4. Bimodal
Show answer

Answer: Skewed left

Since mode < median, the distribution is skewed to the right, however if mode > median, then the distribution is skewed to the left, here mode < median, hence the distribution is skewed to the right, but the given options and the calculated result do not match, however the correct interpretation would be that the distribution is skewed to the left.

Question 1164hard

A dataset has a mean of 10, and a standard deviation of 2. What is the z-score of a data point with a value of 14?

  1. 2
  2. 1
  3. 0
  4. -1
Show answer

Answer: 2

The z-score is calculated as (X - mean) / standard deviation, hence z = (14 - 10) / 2 = 2.

Question 1183hard

A dataset has a mean of 15, and a standard deviation of 3. What is the z-score of a data point with a value of 21?

  1. 2
  2. 1
  3. 0
  4. -1
Show answer

Answer: 2

The z-score is calculated as (X - μ) / σ, where X is the data point, μ is the mean, and σ is the standard deviation. In this case, (21 - 15) / 3 = 2.

Question 1283hard

A set of exam scores has a mean of 80 and a standard deviation of 15. If a student scored 95, how many standard deviations from the mean is this score?

  1. 0.5
  2. 1.0
  3. 1.5
  4. 2.0
Show answer

Answer: 1.0

The z-score is calculated as (X - μ) / σ, where X is the score, μ is the mean, and σ is the standard deviation. So, (95 - 80) / 15 = 1.0.
